8 min
Conditional Rescission and the Buyer as Representative in Creditor's Rights
Conditions for rescission and intra-Hanafi dispute on buyer as representative

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which creditors may rescind a sale of a permitted slave and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the buyer can be a representative when the seller absconds.

Core Idea
The buyer is not a representative for creditors when the seller absconds, unless the buyer confesses the debt.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary addresses two connected issues: first, the specific conditions under which creditors may rescind the sale of a permitted slave by the master; second, what happens when the seller absconds after the sale. The core dispute is intra-Hanafi: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the buyer cannot be sued as a representative (khasm) if he denies the debt, while Abu Yusuf allows it. Understanding this difference is crucial for knowing how creditors can enforce their rights when the seller is unavailable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for rescission
Read the first part of the passage and list the three conditions that must be met for creditors to rescind the sale: the debt is due, the sale was not at their request, and the price is insufficient to cover the debt. Note also when rescission is not allowed (deferred debt, sale at their request, sufficient price).
This sets the background before the dispute.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Find the sentence that begins 'fain ghaaba al-baa’i' and identify the two positions: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad vs. Abu Yusuf. Note the exact issue: when the seller absconds and the buyer denies the debt, can the buyer be a representative for the creditors?
The dispute is only when the buyer denies; if he confesses, rescission is unanimous.
3
Analyze the proofs for each position
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that rescission is a claim against the seller, not the buyer, and the buyer is not an agent. Abu Yusuf argues that the buyer claims ownership and possesses the slave, so he can be a representative like any possessor. Understand the logic of each.
The analogy with pre-emption (shuf'a) is used to support the majority view.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
According to the majority, creditors must wait for the seller or hold him liable for the value. According to Abu Yusuf, they can directly sue the buyer for the debt. Identify which position is mufta bihi and why.
The majority view is the relied-upon position.
5
Apply the ruling to the case of buyer's absence
Note the consensus (ijma) that if the buyer absconds, the seller is not a representative. The creditors can only hold the seller liable for the value. This completes the picture.
This is a separate but related rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن باع سيده إلخ : أي إن باع العبد المأذون سيده والحال أنه قد أعلم المشتري بالدين، فللغرماء رد البيع؛ لأن حقهم تعلق به وهو حق الاستسعاء، أو الاستيفاء من رقبته وفي كل منهما فائدة، فالأول تام مؤخر، والثاني ناقص معجل وبالبيع تفوت هذه الخيرة، فكان لهم ،رده وفائدة الإعلام بالدين سقوط خيار المشتري في الرد بعيب الدين، حتى يلزم البيع في حق المتعاقدين، وإن لم يكن لازما في حق الغرماء، هذا إذا كان الدين حالا، وكان البيع من غير طلب الغرماء، والثمن لا يفي بدينهم، وأما إذا كان دينهم مؤجلا، فالبيع جائز؛ لأنه باع وهو قادر على تسليمه، ولم يتعلق به حق لغيره؛ لأن حق الغرماء متأخر، وكذا إذا كان البيع بطلبهم؛ لأن البيع وقع لأجلهم، وكذا إذا كان الثمن يفي بدينهم رمز الحقائق: ٣٢٢/٢] فإن غاب البائع إلخ: يعني لو باع المولى عبده المأذون المديون، وقبض الثمن، وسلمه إلى المشتري، ثم غاب البائع لا يكون المشتري خصما للغرماء إذا أنكر الدين، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد محملا ، وقال أبو يوسف له: يكون المشتري خصما، ويقضى لهم بديونهم، وعلى هذا الخلاف إذا اشترى دارا ووهبها وسلمها إليه، ثم غاب ثم حضر الشفيع، فالموهوب له لا يكون خصما عندهما، خلافا له، هو يقول: إن ذا اليد يدعي الملك لنفسه في العين، فالمشتري ليس بخصم لهم. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٠٨/٨] وإنما قلنا: إذا أنكر المشتري الدين؛ لأنه إذا أقر بديونهم وصدقهم، كان للغرماء أن يردوا البيع بلا خلاف، هذا إذا غاب البائع، وإن غاب المشتري، فالبائع ليس بخصم إجماعا حتى يحضر المشتري؛ لأن الملك واليد له، ولا يمكن إبطالهما وهو غائب، لكن لهم تضمين البائع قيمته؛ لأنه صار مفوتا حقهم، فإذا ضمنوه القيمة جاز البيع، ويكون الثمن للبائع، وإن اختاروا إجازة البيع أخذوا الثمن. (عيني، فتح، ملا مسكين)
If the master sold etc.: That is, if the master sold the permitted slave while he had informed the buyer of the debt, then the creditors may rescind the sale, because their right is attached to him, namely the right to seek earnings or to take from his value, and in each there is benefit; the first is complete but deferred, the second is deficient but immediate, and by the sale this choice is lost, so they have the right to rescind. The benefit of informing the buyer is to preclude the buyer's option to return due to the defect of debt, so the sale becomes binding between the contracting parties, even if not binding regarding the creditors. This is when the debt is due, the sale is not at the creditors' request, and the price does not cover their debt. If their debt is deferred, the sale is valid because he sold while able to deliver and no one else's right was attached (since creditors' right is later). Similarly if the sale was at their request, and if the price covers their debt. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/322] If the seller is absent etc.: That is, if the master sold his indebted permitted slave, received the price, delivered him to the buyer, then the seller absconds, the buyer is not a representative (khasm) for the creditors if he denies the debt. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: The buyer is a representative, and the creditors may have their debts adjudged from him. The same difference exists if someone bought a house, gifted it, delivered it, then the seller absconds and the pre-emptor appears: the donee is not a representative according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contrary to him (Abu Yusuf). He says: The possessor claims ownership for himself in the thing, so the buyer is not a representative for them. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 8/208) We say: if the buyer denies the debt; because if he confesses their debts and affirms them, the creditors may rescind the sale without disagreement. This is if the seller is absent. If the buyer is absent, the seller is not a representative by consensus until the buyer appears, because ownership and possession belong to him, and they cannot be invalidated in his absence. However, they may hold the seller liable for its value, because he has squandered their right. If they hold him liable for the value, the sale is valid and the price goes to the seller. If they choose to confirm the sale, they take the price. (Ayni, Fath, Mulla Miskin)
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of creditors' rights after the master sells the permitted slave. It first clarifies the conditions under which the creditors may rescind: when the debt is due, the sale was not at their request, and the price is insufficient. If the debt is deferred, or the sale was at their request, or the price covers the debt, the sale is valid and they cannot rescind. Then it addresses the case where the seller absconds after receiving the price. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the majority of the Hanafi school), the buyer is not a valid representative (khasm) for the creditors if he denies the debt. Abu Yusuf disagrees, holding that the buyer is a representative because he claims ownership. The analogy with pre-emption (shuf'a) supports the majority view. If the buyer confesses the debt, the creditors may rescind without dispute. If the buyer absconds, the seller is not a representative; the creditors may only hold the seller liable for the value. This intra-Hanafi dispute has practical implications for how creditors pursue their rights.

Key Terms
خصم (khaṣm): A representative or litigant who can be sued in place of the absent party; the text discusses whether the buyer can be a khasm for the absent seller.
شفعة (shuf'a): Pre-emption right; the analogy used to show that the buyer is not a representative in the absence of the seller.
تضمين (taḍmīn): Holding liable for the value; the creditors can hold the seller liable for the value of the slave if he absconds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, when the seller of a permitted slave absconds and the buyer denies the debt, can the creditors sue the buyer as a representative?
A) Yes, the buyer is always a representative.
B) No, the buyer is not a representative.
C) Only if the buyer confesses the debt.
D) Only if the seller is present.

Key Takeaway
Creditors cannot sue the buyer for rescission when the seller absconds and the buyer denies the debt; they must pursue the seller.

Istihsan over Qiyas: The Slave Trader's Claim
Ruling with proof based on istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting a slave trader's claim of permission and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas.

Core Idea
Istihsan validates a slave's trade permission due to necessity, despite qiyas requiring proof.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a practical market scenario: a person claims to be a slave of Zayd and engages in trade. According to strict qiyas (analogy), his word would not be accepted without evidence. However, the Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) to validate his transactions, relying on necessity and the consensus of Muslims. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this ruling and its limits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Case and Its Two Scenarios
The passage describes a person arriving in a city claiming to be a slave of Zayd. He buys and sells. The case has two subcases: (1) he explicitly says his master permitted him, (2) he trades without mentioning permission. In both, istihsan accepts the permission, making transactions binding.
Distinguishing the explicit vs. implicit claim is key to understanding the ruling's scope.
2
Contrast Qiyas vs. Istihsan
Qiyas would require proof (al-bayyina) for the claim, so the slave would not be believed. Istihsan overrides this due to necessity (darura) and common practice (balwa), as requiring proof every time is impractical.
Qiyas is the default; istihsan is a stronger proof when conditions justify it.
3
Examine the Basis of Istihsan
The basis is twofold: (1) consensus of Muslims (ijma) – people deal with such traders without demanding proof, and (2) necessity – permission is essential for valid trade, but verifying at every transaction is impossible. The maxim 'what is constrained upon people is given wider scope' applies.
Istihsan is not speculation; it is grounded in revealed sources (ijma) and public interest.
4
Understand the Scope: Debts and the Slave’s Person
If debts exceed earnings, the slave’s person (raqabah) cannot be sold because it belongs to the master. Only the slave’s earnings (kasb) are liable. This protects the master’s property rights.
The ruling balances creditors’ rights with master’s ownership.
5
Role of the Master’s Confession or Denial
If the master appears and confirms the permission, the slave can be sold. If he denies, the creditors must prove permission; otherwise, they wait until the slave is freed.
The master’s testimony shifts the burden of proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قدم مصرا إلخ : أي أتى رجل مصرا من الأمصار ، وادعى أنه عبد زيد، فاشترى وباع، لزمه كل شيء من التجارة، ويقبل قوله في الإذن في حق كسبه حتى تقضى بها ديونه والمسألة على وجهين: أحدهما: أن يخبر أن المولى أذن له فيصدق ،استحسانا عدلا كان أو غير ،عدل والقياس أن لا يصدق. وجه الاستحسان: أن الناس يعاملونه من غير اشتراط شيء من ذلك، وإجماع المسلمين حجة يخص بها الأثر، ويترك بها القياس، ولأن في ذلك ضرورة ،وبلوى فإن الإذن لابد منه لصحة تصرفه، وإقامة الحجة عند كل عقد غير ممكن، وما ضاق على الناس أمره اتسع حكمه، وما عمت بليته اتسعت قضيته، والثاني: أن يبيع ويشتري ولا يخبر بشيء، ففي الاستحسان يثبت إذنه؛ لأن الظاهر أنه مأذون؛ لأن عقله ودينه يمنعه عن ارتكاب المحرم؛ لأن الظاهر هو الأصل، فيعمل به فصح تصرفاته تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٠٩/٨] ولا يباع إلخ : يعني إذا لزمته ديون ولم يكن في كسبه وفاء لا تباع رقبته؛ لأنها ملك المولى، فلا يصدق فيه، ولا يلزم من وجوب الدين عليه أن تباع فيه كما لو كان المديون مدبرا أو أم ولد بخلاف الكسب؛ فإن المولى لا يملكه. تكملة البحر الرائق: ۲۰۹/۸] فإن حضر وأقر بإذنه إلخ : يعني إذا حضر المولى وأقر بإذنه بيع العبد في الدين؛ لظهور الدين في حقه بإقراره وإلا لا يعني وإن لم يقر بإذنه بل قال: إنه محجور لا يباع، والقول قوله، وعلى الغرماء البينة، فإن أقاموا يباع، وإلا لا، ويطالب بعد العتق. (ملتقط من التكملة، ملا مسكين)
And whoever comes to a city etc.: That is, a man comes to a city and claims that he is the slave of Zayd, then buys and sells; every transaction is binding upon him, and his statement regarding permission is accepted concerning his earnings, so that his debts may be satisfied. The case has two aspects: First, he informs that the master permitted him; he is believed by istihsan, whether he is just or not. By qiyas he would not be believed. The basis of istihsan is that people deal with him without stipulating any of that, and the consensus of the Muslims is a proof that overrides an athar (tradition) and abandons qiyas. Also because there is necessity and common affliction: permission is necessary for the validity of his dealings, and establishing proof at every transaction is impossible, and what is constrained upon people is given wider scope, and what is widespread in affliction is given a broad ruling. Second, he buys and sells without informing anything; by istihsan his permission is established, because the apparent state indicates he is permitted, since his reason and religion prevent him from committing wrong, and the apparent is the basis, so it is acted upon, and his transactions are valid. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 8/209) And he is not sold etc.: That is, if debts are incurred and his earnings are insufficient, his person (raqabah) is not sold, because it is the master's property, so he is not believed regarding it, nor does liability for debt necessitate being sold, just as if the debtor was a mudabbar or umm walad. Unlike earnings, because the master does not own them. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 8/209) If the master appears and confesses his permission etc.: That is, if the master appears and confesses the permission, the slave is sold for the debt because the debt becomes apparent against him by his confession. Otherwise, meaning if he does not confess but says the slave is interdicted (mahjur), he is not sold, and the master's word is accepted; the creditors must bring evidence; if they do, he is sold; otherwise not, and they claim after the slave's freedom. (Compiled from al-Takmila, Mulla Miskin)
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage addresses the case of a person who appears in a city claiming to be a slave of someone and engages in trade. According to istihsan (juristic preference), his claim of permission from his master is accepted, and his transactions are valid and binding. This is contrary to qiyas (analogy), which would require proof. The reason for istihsan is necessity and common practice: people deal with him without checking, and consensus supports this. The text presents two scenarios: one where he explicitly states permission, and one where he does not; in both, istihsan establishes permission based on the apparent situation. However, if debts exceed his earnings, his person cannot be sold because it belongs to the master; the creditors cannot force sale of the slave's body, only his earnings. If the master later appears and confirms the permission, the slave can be sold. If the master denies, the creditors must prove the permission; otherwise, they must wait until the slave is freed.

Key Terms
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas in cases of necessity or due to consensus; here used to accept the claim of a person who appears as a slave without proof.
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning; the default method that would require proof for the claim, but is set aside here by istihsan.
ضرورة (ḍarūra): Necessity that makes stringent rules easier; a basis for istihsan.
إجماع (ijmāʿ): Consensus of the Muslim community; here cited as evidence for accepting the slave's claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school accept a person's claim that he is a permitted slave without proof?
A) A specific Hadith explicitly allows it.
B) Because of istihsan based on necessity and consensus.
C) Because the slave is always considered trustworthy.
D) Because the master's permission is presumed unless denied.

Key Takeaway
Istihsan permits accepting a slave trader's claim of permission due to necessity and consensus, even though qiyas would require proof.

Permission for a Minor Slave to Trade – Hanafi vs Shafi'i
States permissibility of minor slave trade with Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on permitting a minor slave to trade and identify the opposing Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
A minor slave's trade is valid with the master's permission; Shafi'i disagrees due to lack of capacity.

This lesson examines a short but significant inter-madhhab dispute: can a master permit a minor slave to engage in trade? The Hanafi school affirms this based on the guardian's authority, while Imam al-Shafi'i considers such transactions invalid. Understanding this difference clarifies the scope of legal capacity (ahliyyah) in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between adult and minor slaves
Note that the permission of an adult sane slave is valid by consensus. The dispute arises only for the minor or insane slave.
The passage explicitly mentions this contrast.
2
Identify the point of ikhtilaf
The disagreement is whether the master's permission can make a minor slave's transactions legally effective. Hanafi says yes, Shafi'i says no.
3
Memorise the Hanafi ruling
The Hanafi position: permission is valid and the minor's purchases and sales are binding. The master acts as guardian.
This ruling is from the relied-upon Hanafi view.
4
Memorise the opposing view
Shafi'i holds that the minor lacks legal capacity (ahliyyat al-ada'), so any transaction is void regardless of permission.
The exact dalil is not given but stems from Shafi'i usul.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
In a Hanafi jurisdiction, a master may delegate trade to a minor slave; in Shafi'i, such transactions would be invalid and must be rescinded.
Practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أذن للصبي إلخ: لما فرغ من بيان إذن العبد شرع في بيان الصبي والمعتوه، وقدم الأول؛ لكثرة وقوعه، ولأن إذن العبد صحيح اتفاقا بخلاف إذن الصبي، فإن فيه خلاف الشافعي كذا في "الديري". (فتح)
And if he permits the child etc.: When he finished explaining the permission of the slave, he began to explain the child and the insane, and he presented the first due to its frequent occurrence, and because the permission of the slave is valid by consensus unlike the permission of the child, for in it there is a difference with al-Shafi'i, as in al-Dayri. Commentary
This short passage concludes the section on the permitted slave (ma'dhun) by addressing the case of a minor (sabi) or insane (ma'tuh) slave. The author notes that the permission of an adult sane slave is valid by consensus of the schools. However, permission for a minor slave is a matter of disagreement: the Hanafi school considers it valid, while Imam al-Shafi'i does not. The Hanafi position is that a minor's transactions are effective with the guardian's permission, and the master acts as guardian. The passage refers to al-Dayri and Fath al-Qadir for further details. This ruling is essential for understanding the scope of the master's authority over a minor slave's trade.

Key Terms
صبي (ṣabiyy): A minor child; the text discusses whether his permission to trade is valid when granted by the master.
معتوه (ma'tūh): An insane or mentally deficient person; mentioned alongside the minor as having similar rulings.

The Legal Status of the Ma'dhun (Permitted Minor/Insane Person)
Defining the legal capacity of a permitted minor or insane person in trade

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal status of a permitted minor or insane person (ma'dhun) in Hanafi fiqh, classify their actions into three categories, and identify when guardian permission is required.

Core Idea
A permitted minor or insane person who understands trade is like a permitted slave — their transactions are valid within the scope of permission.

This lesson introduces the ma'dhun (permitted person) and explains their legal capacity in trade. In Hanafi law, a minor or insane person who has some understanding of commerce can be given permission by their guardian to transact. They are treated similarly to a permitted slave, with an important exception: the guardian retains certain powers and duties. The text also categorises all actions of such individuals into three types: those that are purely beneficial, those that are purely harmful, and those that are ambiguous. Understanding this classification is key to determining which actions require guardian permission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the permission condition
Read the opening sentence: 'The insane person who understands buying and selling, his guardian (gives permission), so he in buying and selling is like a permitted slave.' Note that the permission is from the guardian (wali), and the person must have some understanding of trade.
The term 'ma'tuh' is used for an insane person with partial understanding, not a complete lunatic.
2
Understand the analogy to a permitted slave
The text equates the permitted minor/insane person to a 'abd ma'dhun (permitted slave) in most rulings: their transactions are executed (nafidh), they are not restricted to a specific trade type, they can even sell with exorbitant fraud according to Imam Abu Hanifa, etc.
This analogy indicates that the person has legal capacity in trade despite being under guardianship.
3
Analyze the three categories of actions
The text states that the actions of a minor or insane person are of three types: (1) purely beneficial (like accepting Islam) – no permission needed; (2) purely harmful (like divorce or freeing a slave) – never valid even with compensation; (3) ambiguous (like sale, purchase, marriage) – requires guardian permission.
This classification is Hanafi-specific and determines the scope of the permission.
4
Note the requirement of understanding trade
The ma'dhun must understand that sale removes ownership and purchase brings it, and must intend profit and distinguish slight from exorbitant fraud. This understanding is a condition for the validity of the permission.
If the person lacks this understanding, permission would be meaningless.

Source Text

أحكام المأذون
والمعتوه الذي يعقل البيع والشراء وليّه فهو في الشراء والبيع كالعبد المأذون.

في جميع ما ذكرنا من الأحكام
الذي يعقل إلخ صفة لكل من الصبي والمعتوه لا للمعتوه فقط كذا في "الحموي". (فتح) فهو في الشراء إلخ: أي كل واحد من الصبي والمعتوه الذين أذن لهما وليهما في التجارة كالعبد المأذون في أحكام الشراء والبيع فينفذ تصرفه، ولا يتقيد بنوع من التجارات دون نوع، ويكون مأذونا بالسكوت حين يراه يبيع ويشتري، وصح إقراره بما في يده من كسبه ويجوز بيعه بالغبن الفاحش عند الإمام، خلافا لهما، إلى غير ذلك الأحكام التي ذكرها في العبد المأذون، والمراد بكونه يعقل البيع أن يعلم أن البيع سالب للملك، والشراء جالب وأنه يقصد به الربح ويعرف الغبن اليسير من الفاحش، وقال الشافعي: لا تنفذ تصرفاته، وبيان الدلائل الجانبين مذكور في المطولات تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢١٠/٨] قال في "الفتح": وللصبي والمعتوه أن يأذن لعبده أيضا؛ لأن الإذن في التجارة تجارة معنى، بخلاف ما إذا أذن المعتوه لابنه، حيث لا يصح؛ لأنه مولى عليه، فلا يلي على غيره، وكذا لا يملك الصبي ولا المعتوه المأذون لهما أن يتزوجا أو يزوجا مماليكهما إلا بإذن الولي بالتزوج أو تزويج الأمة لا العبد. واعلم أن تصرفات الصبي والمعتوه على ثلاثة أقسام الأول: ما لا يتوقف نفاذه على الإذن؛ لكونه نفعا كالإسلام، الثاني: ما لا ينفذ أصلا ولو بالإجارة؛ لكونه ضررا كالطلاق والعتاق وغيرهما ولو على مال، والثالث: ما احتمل النفع والضرر، فيتوقف على الإذن من الولي كالبيع والشراء والنكاح. (باختصار) كالعبد إلخ: أي في جميع الأحكام، إلا أن الولي لا يمنع من التصرف في مالهما وإن كان عليهما دين، ولا يقبل إقراره عليهما وإن لم يكن عليهما دين بخلاف المولى، والفرق أن إقرار الولي عليهما شهادة؛ لأنه إقرار على غيره فلا يقبل، ودينهما غير متعلق بمالهما، وإنما هو في الذمة؛ لأنهما حران [تبيين الحقائق: ٣١٢/٦] واعلم أنه لا خلاف في صحة الإذن للمعتوه الذي يعقل البيع والشراء إذا بلغ معتوها، أما من بلغ عاقلا ثم عته، ففيه خلاف قال البلخي: لا يصح إذنه قياسا، وهو قول أبي يوسف لله، ويصح استحسانا، وهو قول محمد الله، وهذا بخلاف ما إذا عته الأب أو جُنّ، فإنه لا يثبت للابن الكبير ولاية التصرف في ماله، وإنما يثبت له ولاية التزويج، كذا في "الزيلعي". (فتح الله المعين)
Book of the Permitted (Ma'dhun). Rulings of the Ma'dhun. The insane person (ma'tuh) who understands buying and selling, his guardian (gives permission), so he in buying and selling is like a permitted slave. The subject of 'idhn' applies to all the rulings we have mentioned. 'Who understands' etc. is a description for both the minor and the insane, not only for the insane - as in al-Hamawi. (Fath) So he in buying and selling etc.: meaning each of the minor and the insane to whom their guardian has given permission for trade is like a permitted slave in the rulings of buying and selling: his transaction is executed, he is not restricted to a type of trade without another, and he is considered permitted by silence when the guardian sees him buying and selling, his admission regarding what is in his hand from his earnings is valid, and his sale with exorbitant fraud is permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and other rulings mentioned for a permitted slave. The meaning of 'he understands buying' is that he knows that sale removes ownership and purchase brings it, and he intends profit and knows slight fraud from exorbitant. Al-Shafi'i said: his transactions are not executed, and the explanation of the proofs of both sides is mentioned in lengthy works. It is said in al-Fath: The minor and the insane may also give permission to their slave, because permission in trade is trade in meaning, unlike when an insane person gives permission to his son, where it is not valid because he is under guardianship, so he cannot be guardian over others. Similarly, a permitted minor or insane person does not have the capacity to marry or marry off their slaves except with the permission of the guardian for marriage or marrying off a female slave, not a male slave. Know that the actions of a minor and an insane person are of three types: first: what does not depend on permission for its execution, because it is beneficial like embracing Islam; second: what is never executed even by compensation, because it is harmful like divorce, emancipation, and others even for money; third: what is possibly beneficial or harmful, so it depends on permission from the guardian, like sale, purchase, and marriage. (Briefly) 'Like a slave' etc.: meaning in all rulings, except that the guardian is not prevented from disposing of their wealth even if they have debt, and his admission against them is not accepted even if they have no debt, contrary to the master. The difference is that the guardian's admission against them is testimony, because it is an admission against others, so it is not accepted; and their debt is not attached to their wealth, but is in the dhimmah because they are free. Know that there is no dispute about the validity of permission for an insane person who understands buying and selling if he was born insane. However, if he reached maturity sane then became insane, there is dispute: al-Balkhi said his permission is not valid by qiyas, and that is the saying of Abu Yusuf, and it is valid by istihsan, and that is the saying of Muhammad. This is unlike when the father becomes insane or mad, then the adult son does not have guardianship over his wealth, but he has guardianship over marriage, as in al-Zayla'i. (Fath al-Mu'in)
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Ma'dhun defines the legal status of a minor (sabi) or insane person (ma'tuh) who is given permission (idhn) by their guardian to engage in trade. The ruling is that such a person is treated like a permitted slave (abd ma'dhun) in most aspects of trade, including that their transactions are executed, they are not restricted to a specific type of trade, and they can even make sales involving ghabn fahish (exorbitant fraud) according to Imam Abu Hanifa, unlike the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The passage explains that the person must understand the purpose of trade: that sale removes ownership, purchase brings it, and they intend profit and can distinguish slight from exorbitant fraud. It also mentions that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees entirely, holding that their transactions are not executed. The text then discusses three categories of actions: those that are purely beneficial (like accepting Islam) and do not need permission; those that are purely harmful (like divorce or freeing a slave) and are never valid even if done for compensation; and those that are ambiguous (like sale, purchase, and marriage) which require guardian permission. Additionally, the passage covers an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding an insane person who was sane at maturity and then became insane: according to Abu Yusuf, his permission for subsequent trades is invalid by qiyas, while according to Muhammad it is valid by istihsan. The preferred position is not explicitly stated here but is a matter of tarjih. The passage also clarifies differences with a slave ma'dhun: the guardian is not prevented from disposing of their wealth even if they have debt, and the guardian's admission (iqrar) against them is not accepted because it is testimony against another. The overall ruling is that a permitted minor or insane person has significant legal capacity in trade, but with important limitations.

Key Terms
المأذون (al-ma'dhun): A person (minor or insane) who has been given permission by his guardian to engage in trade.
المعتوه (al-ma'tuh): An insane person who has some understanding (ya'qil) of buying and selling, not completely insane.
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghabn al-fahish): Exorbitant fraud or deception in price where the buyer or seller is cheated beyond what is customary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following actions of a permitted minor does NOT require guardian permission?
A) Selling a bicycle
B) Buying groceries
C) Accepting Islam
D) Marrying

Key Takeaway
A permitted minor or insane person (ma'dhun) who understands trade is legally capable of transacting within the scope of guardian permission, with transactions being generally valid except for purely harmful acts.

intermediate
6 min
Disputes on the Ma'dhun: Exorbitant Fraud and Permission After Insanity
Intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab disputes on the ma'dhun's capacity and permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the intra-Hanafi disputes on sales with ghabn fahish and the validity of permission for a person who becomes insane after maturity, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf for each.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa allows the ma'dhun to sell with exorbitant fraud; the Sahibayn prohibit it. Permission given when sane remains valid by istihsan if later insanity occurs.

This lesson focuses on two specific disputes within the Hanafi school relating to the ma'dhun. The first concerns whether a sale involving exorbitant fraud (ghabn fahish) by a permitted minor or insane person is valid. The second deals with the validity of permission for trade given by a person who was sane at maturity but later becomes insane. These questions highlight the balance between facilitating trade and protecting the vulnerable. We also note the opposition of Imam al-Shafi'i to the very concept of capacity for such individuals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first dispute: ghabn fahish
Read the part: 'ويجوز بيعه بالغبن الفاحش عند الإمام، خلافا لهما'. This tells us that Imam Abu Hanifa permitted the ma'dhun to sell with exorbitant fraud, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad held it invalid.
The dispute is about whether the transaction is binding or can be nullified due to excessive deception.
2
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf for ghabn fahish
If Imam's view is taken, the sale is valid and the buyer keeps the item, even if the price was unfair. If the Sahibayn's view is taken, the sale is invalid and can be rescinded.
The dispute reflects different approaches to protecting the ma'dhun's wealth.
3
Identify the second dispute: permission after insanity
The text states: 'أما من بلغ عاقلا ثم عته، ففيه خلاف'. Al-Balkhi and Abu Yusuf say the permission is invalid by qiyas; Muhammad says it is valid by istihsan.
The distinction is between being born insane (ittifaq) and becoming insane after maturity (ikhtilaf).
4
Understand the basis of each view
Abu Yusuf uses qiyas: since the person is now insane, he cannot give valid consent. Muhammad uses istihsan: the permission was given when he had capacity, and it should not be automatically revoked by subsequent insanity.
Istihsan here considers the continuity of trade and the original validity.
5
Consider the Shafi'i opposition
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the transactions of a minor or insane person are not executed at all, even with permission. This is a more fundamental disagreement.
The proofs are mentioned in lengthy works (mutilat).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

والمعتوه الذي يعقل البيع والشراء وليّه فهو في الشراء والبيع كالعبد المأذون.
من
من
فاعل أذن
في جميع ما ذكرنا من الأحكام
الذي يعقل إلخ صفة لكل من الصبي والمعتوه لا للمعتوه فقط كذا في "الحموي". (فتح) فهو في الشراء إلخ: أي كل واحد من الصبي والمعتوه الذين أذن لهما وليهما في التجارة كالعبد المأذون في أحكام الشراء والبيع فينفذ تصرفه، ولا يتقيد بنوع من التجارات دون نوع، ويكون مأذونا بالسكوت حين يراه يبيع ويشتري، وصح إقراره بما في يده من كسبه ويجوز بيعه بالغبن الفاحش عند الإمام، خلافا لهما، إلى غير ذلك الأحكام التي ذكرها في العبد المأذون، والمراد بكونه يعقل البيع أن يعلم أن البيع سالب للملك، والشراء جالب وأنه يقصد به الربح ويعرف الغبن اليسير من الفاحش، وقال الشافعي: لا تنفذ تصرفاته، وبيان الدلائل الجانبين مذكور في المطولات تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢١٠/٨] قال في "الفتح": وللصبي والمعتوه أن يأذن لعبده أيضا؛ لأن الإذن في التجارة تجارة معنى، بخلاف ما إذا أذن المعتوه لابنه، حيث لا يصح؛ لأنه مولى عليه، فلا يلي على غيره، وكذا لا يملك الصبي ولا المعتوه المأذون لهما أن يتزوجا أو يزوجا مماليكهما إلا بإذن الولي بالتزوج أو تزويج الأمة لا العبد. واعلم أن تصرفات الصبي والمعتوه على ثلاثة أقسام الأول: ما لا يتوقف نفاذه على الإذن؛ لكونه نفعا كالإسلام، الثاني: ما لا ينفذ أصلا ولو بالإجارة؛ لكونه ضررا كالطلاق والعتاق وغيرهما ولو على مال، والثالث: ما احتمل النفع والضرر، فيتوقف على الإذن من الولي كالبيع والشراء والنكاح. Definition and Conditions of Ghasb
Defining ghasb linguistically and technically with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi technical definition of ghasb and identify the conditions that must be present for an act to be considered ghasb.

Core Idea
Ghasb is establishing a wrongful hand over someone's property — but only if it is valuable, protected, transferable, and taken openly.

In this lesson, we examine the precise definition of ghasb (usurpation) according to the Hanafi school. The author defines it as 'removing the rightful hand by establishing the wrongful hand,' but this definition requires several conditions to be met. Understanding these conditions is crucial to differentiate ghasb from theft, and to determine liability for the usurper.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic meaning of ghasb
In Arabic, ghasb means taking something from another by force, whether property or otherwise.
The language includes taking a free person, which is not valuable.
2
Extract the technical definition from the text
The technical definition: removing the rightful hand by establishing a wrongful hand over a valuable, protected, transferable property without permission.
The definition adds conditions beyond the linguistic meaning.
3
List the conditions mentioned in the text
The text specifies: valuable (mutaqawwim), protected (muhtaram), transferable (qabil lil-naql), and not secret (to exclude theft).
Non-valuable like wine, non-protected like harbi property, immovable, and secret taking are excluded.
4
Explain why each condition is necessary
Each condition excludes certain cases: non-valuable goods are not property; non-protected goods have no legal sanctity; immovable property cannot be physically usurped in the same way; secret taking is theft and has different rulings.
The usurper is not liable for increments or attached items without his act.
5
State the ruling of ghasb
Ghasb is haram (sin) for one who knows; the usurper must return the property if it exists or pay compensation if it is destroyed, even if he was unaware of the ownership.
The text also discusses that compensation is only paid upon destruction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الغصب تعريف الغصب وحكمه
كتاب الغصب
هو إزالة اليد المحقة بإثبات اليد المبطلة
الكائنة على الباطل
وجه
كتاب الغصب أورد الغصب بعد الإذن في التجارة لوجهين أحدهما أن الغصب من أنواع التجارة مآلا حتى صح إقرار المأذون به، كما يصح بدين التجارة، ولم يصح بدين المهر؛ لأنه ليس من التجارة، الثاني: أن المغصوب ما دام قائما بعينه لا يكون الغاصب مالكا لرقبته فصار كالعبد المأذون فإنه غير مالك لرقبته وما في يده من مال التجارة، إلا أنه قدم الإذن في التجارة؛ لأنه مشروع من كل وجه، والغصب ليس بمشروع، كذا في "النهاية"، وفي هذه المناسبة نظر، فإن الغصب عبارة عن إزالة اليد والإزالة ليست من أنواع التجارة، والذي أرى أن المناسبة ما ذكره صاحب "غاية البيان" حيث قال: المأذون يتصرف في الشيء بالإذن الشرعي، والغاصب يتصرف لا بالإذن الشرعي، فبينهما مناسبة المقابلة تكملة البحر الرائق: ۲۱٤/٨] ثم الغصب في اللغة: أخذ الشيء من الغير على وجه القهر مالا كان أو غيره، حتى يقال على أخذ الحر ونحوه مما لا يتقوم، يقال: غصبته منه، وغصبته عليه، وفي الشرع : ما بينه بقوله: "هو إزالة اليد المحقة إلخ". [رمز الحقائق: ٣٢٤/٢] هو إزالة إلخ من أحق أي الكائنة على الحق] أي الغصب في اصطلاح الشرع: إزالة اليد التي لها حق بإثبات اليد المبطلة في مال متقوم محترم قابل للنقل بغير إذن مالكه، وهذه القيود لابد منها، فإن الغاصب لا يضمن زوائد المغصوب إذا هلكت بغير تعد؛ لعدم إزالة يد المالك، ولا ما صار مع المغصوب بغير صنعه، كما إذا غصب دابة، فتبعها أخرى أو ولدها، لا يضمن التابع؛ لعدم الصنع فيه، وكذا لا يضمن غير المتقوم كالخمر، أو غير المحترم كمال الحربي في دار الحرب ولا ما لا يقبل النقل كالعقار. وعند محمد الغصب هو تفويت يد الملك لا غيره، وعند الثلاثة إثبات يد مبطلة لا غير، حتى إن الاستخدام أو الحمل على الدابة غصب، لا الجلوس على البساط عندنا وعندهم الجلوس أيضا غصب، وقد أشار الشيخ إلى ذلك بقوله: فالاستخدام إلخ. رمز الحقائق: ٣٢٤/٢] وقال في "الفتح": وثمرة الخلاف بيننا وبين الشافعي تظهر في زوائد المغصوب وثمرة ،البستان، فإنهما لا يضمنان عندنا إذا هلكا بغير صنع الغاصب، خلافا له، انتهى، قال في "ملا مسكين": واعلم أنه لابد أن يزاد على تعريف المصنف: "لا على سبيل الخفية" ليخرج السرقة، وحكم الغصب الاثم لمن علم ورد العين ،قائمة والغرم ،هالكة وإن كان بغير علم بأن ظن أن المأخوذ ماله، أو اشترى عينا ثم ظهر استحقاقه، فالضمان عند هلاك المأخوذ لا غير.
أخذ شيء
بإثبات اليد المبطلة والنسبة بين إزالة اليد وإثباتها بالعموم والخصوص من وجه؛ فإنهما مجتمعان في من يد مالكه بلا ،رضاه ويفترقان في زوائد المغصوب وتبعيد المالك، فإن في الأول يوجد إثبات اليد ولا توجد إزالتها، وفي الثاني بالعكس. (فتح)
Book of Ghasb (Usurpation). Definition and ruling of Ghasb. It is removing the rightful hand by establishing the wrongful hand that is upon falsehood. Reason: The book of Ghasb is placed after the permission for trade for two reasons: one, that ghasb is a type of trade in the final outcome, such that the admission of the permitted regarding it is valid, as it is valid regarding a debt of trade, but not valid regarding a dower debt because it is not from trade; second, that the usurped property as long as it remains in its essence, the usurper is not the owner of its corpus, so it becomes like the permitted slave who is not the owner of his corpus nor the trade capital in his hand, except that permission for trade is placed first because it is legislated in every aspect, while ghasb is not legislated. And in this appropriateness there is consideration, for ghasb is an expression of removal, and removal is not a type of trade. What I see is that the appropriateness is what the author of Ghayat al-Bayan mentioned: the permitted agent acts with the permission of the Shari'a, while the usurper acts without the permission of the Shari'a, so between them is an appropriateness of contrast. Then ghasb in language: taking something from another by force, whether it is property or otherwise, even said of taking a free person and the like of what is not valuable. In Shari'a: what he defined by saying: 'It is removing the rightful hand etc.' i.e., ghasb in the terminology of Shari'a: the removal of the hand that has right by establishing the wrongful hand in a valuable, protected property that is transferable, without the permission of its owner. These restrictions are necessary, because the usurper is not liable for increments of the usurped property if they perish without transgression, due to not removing the owner's hand; nor for what becomes attached to the usurped property without his own act, such as if he usurps a riding animal and another follows it or its offspring, he is not liable for the follower due to no act of his; similarly, he is not liable for non-valuable property like wine, or non-protected property like the wealth of a harbi in dar al-harb, nor for what is not transferable like real estate. According to Muhammad, ghasb is the loss of the hand of ownership and nothing else; according to the three, it is establishing a wrongful hand and nothing else, such that using or loading an animal is ghasb, but sitting on a carpet is not ghasb according to us, while according to them sitting is also ghasb. The author indicated this by his saying: 'so using etc.' It is said in al-Fath: The practical consequence of the difference between us and al-Shafi'i appears in the increments of the usurped property and the fruit of the garden: they are not liable according to us if they perish without the act of the usurper, contrary to him. It is said in Mulla Miskin: Know that it is necessary to add to the definition of the author: 'not in a hidden manner' to exclude theft. The ruling of ghasb is sin for one who knows, and return of the property if it still exists, and compensation if it is destroyed, even if it was without knowledge, as when he thought the taken property was his own, or he bought an item and then it became known that it belonged to someone else; then compensation is only upon destruction of the taken item, not otherwise. 'Taking something by establishing the wrongful hand.' The relationship between removal of the hand and establishment is that of general and specific from one perspective: they meet in the one from whose hand the owner's hand is removed without his consent, and they differ in increments of the usurped property and the removal of the owner: in the first (increments) there is establishment of the hand without removal, and in the second (removal of the owner) the opposite. (Fath)
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Ghasb gives the technical definition of ghasb (usurpation) and its ruling. The author defines ghasb as 'removing the rightful hand by establishing the wrongful hand' but then adds necessary conditions: it must be over a valuable (mutaqawwim), protected (muhtaram), transferable property, without the owner's permission. The passage explains why ghasb is placed after the book of trade: because ultimately ghasb leads to trade, and a ma'dhun's admission regarding a usurped item is valid like a trade debt. It discusses the definitional dispute within the Hanafi school: Imam Muhammad defines ghasb as 'loss of ownership hand' (tafwit yad al-milk), while the other three imams define it as 'establishing a wrongful hand' (ithbat yad mubtila). This difference has practical consequences: for example, using a riding animal is ghasb by all, but sitting on a carpet is ghasb according to the majority (the three) but not according to Muhammad? Actually the text says: 'such that using or loading an animal is ghasb, but sitting on a carpet is not ghasb with us, and with them sitting is also ghasb.' So 'us'=Hanafi school, 'them'=Shafi'i school. So the Hanafi position differentiates between using a riding animal (ghasb) and sitting on a carpet (not ghasb), because using the animal is a form of taking benefit, while sitting on a carpet is mere use without removal. Then the text mentions the difference with al-Shafi'i regarding increments: Hanafis do not hold the usurper liable for increments (like fruit) if they perish without his act, while Shafi'i does. Then a quote from Mulla Miskin adds that the definition must exclude theft (by adding 'not in secret') to differentiate from sariqa. Finally, the ruling: ghasb is a sin for one who knows, and the property must be returned if still extant, or compensation paid if destroyed, even if the person was unaware (like thinking it was his own). The passage ends with a note on the relationship between removal and establishment of the hand.

Key Terms
الغصب (al-ghasb): Usurpation: taking someone's property forcibly and wrongfully.
اليد المحقة (al-yad al-muhiqqa): The rightful hand; the possession of the true owner.
اليد المبطلة (al-yad al-mubtila): The wrongful hand; the possession of the usurper that is invalid and unjust.
السرقة (al-sariqa): Theft; taking property secretly. The text excludes theft from the definition of ghasb by adding the condition 'not secretly'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is a condition for an act to be considered ghasb?
A) The property must be immovable
B) The property must be valuable
C) The taking must be secret
D) The owner must be a Muslim

Key Takeaway
Ghasb is defined as removing the rightful hand by establishing a wrongful hand over valuable, protected, transferable property taken openly, and it is haram with liability to return or compensate.

intermediate

The Intra-Hanafi Definition Dispute: Tafwit vs Ithbat
Intra-Hanafi definition dispute on ghasb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Imam Muhammad's definition of ghasb (tafwit yad al-milk) and the majority definition (ithbat yad mubtila), and identify the practical consequence.

Core Idea
Whether sitting on someone's carpet without damage is ghasb depends on whether you define ghasb as losing ownership or establishing wrongful possession.

The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on the precise definition of ghasb. Imam Muhammad defines it as the loss of the owner's hand (tafwit yad al-milk), while the majority of the school's imams define it as the establishment of a wrongful hand (ithbat yad mubtila). This lesson explores the practical difference this definitional dispute makes in everyday cases.

Guided Path
1
State the majority definition
The three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and perhaps another) define ghasb as establishing a wrongful hand (ithbat yad mubtila).
This definition focuses on the usurper's action of taking control.
2
State Imam Muhammad's definition
Imam Muhammad defines ghasb as the loss of the owner's hand (tafwit yad al-milk).
This definition focuses on the removal of the owner's control.
3
Identify the practical difference
The text gives the example of sitting on a carpet: according to the majority, sitting is ghasb because it establishes a wrongful hand; according to Muhammad, it is not ghasb because the owner's hand is not removed.
Using a riding animal is ghasb by both definitions.
4
Explain why the majority view is preferred
The majority view is more comprehensive (shamel) as it covers cases like sitting where there is wrongful use but no removal.
The text does not provide a direct rebuttal but implies the majority view is relied upon.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is the majority definition, so sitting on a carpet is considered ghasb and compensable.

Source Text

الغصب (al-ghasb): Usurpation: taking someone's property forcibly and wrongfully.

إثبات يد مبطلة (ithbat yad mubtila): Establishment of a wrongful hand; the definition of ghasb according to the majority.

According to the majority Hanafi definition, which of the following is ghasb?

Liability for Increments: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Cross-madhhab dispute on liability for increments in ghasb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the usurper's liability for increments (e.g., fruit of a tree) and contrast it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
If the usurped property produces fruit that perishes without the usurper's act, the Hanafi school does not hold him liable, while the Shafi'i school does.

A key practical issue in ghasb is the liability for increments (fruits, offspring, etc.) that arise from the usurped property. The Hanafi school takes a distinct position: the usurper is not liable for increments that perish without his own act, unlike the Shafi'i school which holds him liable. This lesson examines the disagreement and its basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The issue is whether the usurper must compensate for increments (e.g., fruits of a garden, offspring of an animal) that perish without his direct action.
2
State the Hanafi position
Hanafi: No liability for increments if they perish without the usurper's act. The text says: 'they are not liable according to us if they perish without the act of the usurper.'
The reason is that the usurper has not removed the owner's hand from these increments.
3
State the Shafi'i position
Shafi'i: The usurper is liable for increments even if they perish without his act, because the increments are considered part of the usurped property.
The text says: 'contrary to him.'
4
Explain the basis for the difference
The Hanafi view is based on the definition of ghasb as removal of the owner's hand. Increments come after usurpation, so no removal. Shafi'i likely sees the usurper's possession as covering the property's produce.
The text mentions 'due to not removing the owner's hand for increments.'
5
Note the practical consequence
If a garden is usurped and fruit ripens and rots without the usurper's act, Hanafi says no compensation; Shafi'i requires compensation.

Source Text

الكائنة على الباطل
وجه
كتاب الغصب أورد الغصب بعد الإذن في التجارة لوجهين أحدهما أن الغصب من أنواع التجارة مآلا حتى صح إقرار المأذون به، كما يصح بدين التجارة، ولم يصح بدين المهر؛ لأنه ليس من التجارة، الثاني: أن المغصوب ما دام قائما بعينه لا يكون الغاصب مالكا لرقبته فصار كالعبد المأذون فإنه غير مالك لرقبته وما في يده من مال التجارة، إلا أنه قدم الإذن في التجارة؛ لأنه مشروع من كل وجه، والغصب ليس بمشروع، كذا في "النهاية"، وفي هذه المناسبة نظر، فإن الغصب عبارة عن إزالة اليد والإزالة ليست من أنواع التجارة، والذي أرى أن المناسبة ما ذكره صاحب "غاية البيان" حيث قال: المأذون يتصرف في الشيء بالإذن الشرعي، والغاصب يتصرف لا بالإذن الشرعي، فبينهما مناسبة المقابلة تكملة البحر الرائق: ۲۱٤/٨] ثم الغصب في اللغة: أخذ الشيء من الغير على وجه القهر مالا كان أو غيره، حتى يقال على أخذ الحر ونحوه مما لا يتقوم، يقال: غصبته منه، وغصبته عليه، وفي الشرع : ما بينه بقوله: "هو إزالة اليد المحقة إلخ". [رمز الحقائق: ٣٢٤/٢] هو إزالة إلخ من أحق أي الكائنة على الحق] أي الغصب في اصطلاح الشرع: إزالة اليد التي لها حق بإثبات اليد المبطلة في مال متقوم محترم قابل للنقل بغير إذن مالكه، وهذه القيود لابد منها، فإن الغاصب لا يضمن زوائد المغصوب إذا هلكت بغير تعد؛ لعدم إزالة يد المالك، ولا ما صار مع المغصوب بغير صنعه، كما إذا غصب دابة، فتبعها أخرى أو ولدها، لا يضمن التابع؛ لعدم الصنع فيه، وكذا لا يضمن غير المتقوم كالخمر، أو غير المحترم كمال الحربي في دار الحرب ولا ما لا يقبل النقل كالعقار. وعند محمد الغصب هو تفويت يد الملك لا غيره، وعند الثلاثة إثبات يد مبطلة لا غير، حتى إن الاستخدام أو الحمل على الدابة غصب، لا الجلوس على البساط عندنا وعندهم الجلوس أيضا غصب، وقد أشار الشيخ إلى ذلك بقوله: فالاستخدام إلخ. رمز الحقائق: ٣٢٤/٢] وقال في "الفتح": وثمرة الخلاف بيننا وبين الشافعي تظهر في زوائد المغصوب وثمرة ،البستان، فإنهما لا يضمنان عندنا إذا هلكا بغير صنع الغاصب، خلافا له، انتهى، قال في "ملا مسكين": واعلم أنه لابد أن يزاد على تعريف المصنف: "لا على سبيل الخفية" ليخرج السرقة، وحكم الغصب الاثم لمن علم ورد العين ،قائمة والغرم ،هالكة وإن كان بغير علم بأن ظن أن المأخوذ ماله، أو اشترى عينا ثم ظهر استحقاقه، فالضمان عند هلاك المأخوذ لا غير.
أخذ شيء
بإثبات اليد المبطلة والنسبة بين إزالة اليد وإثباتها بالعموم والخصوص من وجه؛ فإنهما مجتمعان في من يد مالكه بلا ،رضاه ويفترقان في زوائد المغصوب وتبعيد المالك، فإن في الأول يوجد إثبات اليد ولا توجد إزالتها، وفي الثاني بالعكس. (فتح)
Book of Ghasb (Usurpation). Definition and ruling of Ghasb. It is removing the rightful hand by establishing the wrongful hand that is upon falsehood. Reason: The book of Ghasb is placed after the permission for trade for two reasons: one, that ghasb is a type of trade in the final outcome, such that the admission of the permitted regarding it is valid, as it is valid regarding a debt of trade, but not valid regarding a dower debt because it is not from trade; second, that the usurped property as long as it remains in its essence, the usurper is not the owner of its corpus, so it becomes like the permitted slave who is not the owner of his corpus nor the trade capital in his hand, except that permission for trade is placed first because it is legislated in every aspect, while ghasb is not legislated. And in this appropriateness there is consideration, for ghasb is an expression of removal, and removal is not a type of trade. What I see is that the appropriateness is what the author of Ghayat al-Bayan mentioned: the permitted agent acts with the permission of the Shari'a, while the usurper acts without the permission of the Shari'a, so between them is an appropriateness of contrast. Then ghasb in language: taking something from another by force, whether it is property or otherwise, even said of taking a free person and the like of what is not valuable. In Shari'a: what he defined by saying: 'It is removing the rightful hand etc.' i.e., ghasb in the terminology of Shari'a: the removal of the hand that has right by establishing the wrongful hand in a valuable, protected property that is transferable, without the permission of its owner. These restrictions are necessary, because the usurper is not liable for increments of the usurped property if they perish without transgression, due to not removing the owner's hand; nor for what becomes attached to the usurped property without his own act, such as if he usurps a riding animal and another follows it or its offspring, he is not liable for the follower due to no act of his; similarly, he is not liable for non-valuable property like wine, or non-protected property like the wealth of a harbi in dar al-harb, nor for what is not transferable like real estate. According to Muhammad, ghasb is the loss of the hand of ownership and nothing else; according to the three, it is establishing a wrongful hand and nothing else, such that using or loading an animal is ghasb, but sitting on a carpet is not ghasb according to us, while according to them sitting is also ghasb. The author indicated this by his saying: 'so using etc.' It is said in al-Fath: The practical consequence of the difference between us and al-Shafi'i appears in the increments of the usurped property and the fruit of the garden: they are not liable according to us if they perish without the act of the usurper, contrary to him. It is said in Mulla Miskin: Know that it is necessary to add to the definition of the author: 'not in a hidden manner' to exclude theft. The ruling of ghasb is sin for one who knows, and return of the property if it still exists, and compensation if it is destroyed, even if it was without knowledge, as when he thought the taken property was his own, or he bought an item and then it became known that it belonged to someone else; then compensation is only upon destruction of the taken item, not otherwise. 'Taking something by establishing the wrongful hand.' The relationship between removal of the hand and establishment is that of general and specific from one perspective: they meet in the one from whose hand the owner's hand is removed without his consent, and they differ in increments of the usurped property and the removal of the owner: in the first (increments) there is establishment of the hand without removal, and in the second (removal of the owner) the opposite. (Fath)
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Ghasb gives the technical definition of ghasb (usurpation) and its ruling. The author defines ghasb as 'removing the rightful hand by establishing the wrongful hand' but then adds necessary conditions: it must be over a valuable (mutaqawwim), protected (muhtaram), transferable property, without the owner's permission. The passage explains why ghasb is placed after the book of trade: because ultimately ghasb leads to trade, and a ma'dhun's admission regarding a usurped item is valid like a trade debt. It discusses the definitional dispute within the Hanafi school: Imam Muhammad defines ghasb as 'loss of ownership hand' (tafwit yad al-milk), while the other three imams define it as 'establishing a wrongful hand' (ithbat yad mubtila). This difference has practical consequences: for example, using a riding animal is ghasb by all, but sitting on a carpet is ghasb according to the majority (the three) but not according to Muhammad? Actually the text says: 'such that using or loading an animal is ghasb, but sitting on a carpet is not ghasb with us, and with them sitting is also ghasb.' So 'us'=Hanafi school, 'them'=Shafi'i school. So the Hanafi position differentiates between using a riding animal (ghasb) and sitting on a carpet (not ghasb), because using the animal is a form of taking benefit, while sitting on a carpet is mere use without removal. Then the text mentions the difference with al-Shafi'i regarding increments: Hanafis do not hold the usurper liable for increments (like fruit) if they perish without his act, while Shafi'i does. Then a quote from Mulla Miskin adds that the definition must exclude theft (by adding 'not in secret') to differentiate from sariqa. Finally, the ruling: ghasb is a sin for one who knows, and the property must be returned if still extant, or compensation paid if destroyed, even if the person was unaware (like thinking it was his own). The passage ends with a note on the relationship between removal and establishment of the hand.

Key Terms
الغصب (al-ghasb): Usurpation: taking someone's property forcibly and wrongfully.
الزوائد (al-zawa'id): Increments: fruits, offspring, or other produce that arise from the usurped property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the usurper not liable for increments that perish without his act?
A) Because increments are not valuable
B) Because the owner's hand was not removed from the increments
C) Because increments are not protected
D) Because the usurper did not intend to take the increments

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds the usurper liable only for the original property and not for increments that perish without his act, unlike the Shafi'i school.

Usurpation: Return of the Object, Mithl, or Value
Ruling with proof on usurpation remedies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three remedies for usurpation (return of the object, payment of mithl, payment of value) and state the Hanafi position on valuation dates in intra-madhhab disputes.

Core Idea
The usurper must return the exact object; if it perishes, he pays the mithl; if mithl is unavailable, he pays value on the day of litigation.

When someone wrongfully takes another's property, Islamic law imposes a clear remedy: return the exact object if it still exists. But what if it perishes? This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq unpacks the rules for fungible goods (mithli) and non-fungibles, and reveals a key intra-Hanafi dispute about when to assess value. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying compensation claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary obligation
The text states that returning the exact object (ayn) in the same place is wajib. Note the proof from Hadith and Quran.
The obligation is to return the substance, not just any equivalent.
2
Classify the object as mithli or non-mithli
If the object perishes, determine whether it is a fungible (mithli) or non-fungible. Mithli goods have standard units; non-mithli goods differ individually (e.g., animals).
Mithli is defined by market availability in standard measures.
3
Apply the remedy: mithl or value
For mithli that perishes, the usurper pays the mithl (exact equivalent). For non-mithli, he pays the value on the day of usurpation (by consensus).
Value is a surrogate when mithl is not possible.
4
Handle the case of insirim al-mithl
If the mithl becomes unavailable in the market, there is a dispute: Abu Hanifa says value on litigation day; Abu Yusuf says value on usurpation day; Muhammad says value on the day the mithl became unavailable.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa’s view; the mithl remains a debt until judged.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب رد عينه في مكان غصبه على الغاصب أي عين المغصوب غصبه أو مثله إن هلك وهو مثلي، وإن انصرم المثل فقيمته يوم الخصومة، وما لا مثل له كالحيوان والمعدودات فقيمته يوم غصبه رد عينه إلخ: أي يجب على الغاصب رد المغصوب إن كان قائما ؛ لقوله : على اليد ما أخذت حتى ترد" وقوله علي: "لا يحل لأحدكم أن يأخذ مال أخيه لاعبا ولا جادا وإن أخذه فليرده ؛ ولأنه بالأخذ فوت عليه اليد، وهي مقصودة؛ لأن المالك يتوصل بها إلى تحصيل ثمرات الملك من الانتفاع فيجب نسخ فعله دفعا للضرر، ولما كانت القيم تتفاوت باختلاف الأماكن وجب عليه رده بمكان غصبه فيه. (عيني، فتح) أو مثله إن هلك إلخ: أي إن هلك المغصوب يجب عليه أو مثله إن كان مثليا؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاعْتَدُوا عَلَيْهِ بِمِثْلِ مَا اعْتَدَى عَلَيْكُمْ ﴾ (البقرة: ١٩٤) ورد العين هو الموجب الأصلي؛ لأنه أعدل وأكمل، ورد المثل والقيمة مخلص يصار إليه عند تعذر رد العين ولهذا يطالب برد العين قبل الهلاك، ولو أتى بالقيمة أو المثل لا يعتد به؛ لكونه قاصرا، وكذا يبرأ الغاصب برد العين من غير علم المالك بأن سلمه إليه بجهة أخرى، كما إذا وهبه أو أطعمه إياه، فأكله، والمالك لا يدري أنه ملكه، وفي الإطعام خلاف الشافعي. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٢٤/٢] وإن انصرم المثل إلخ: يعني إذا انقطع المثل عن أيدي الناس يجب على الغاصب قيمته يوم الخصومة، وهذا قول الإمام، وقال الثاني يوم الغصب وقال محمد: يوم الانقطاع؛ لأن المثل هو الواجب والقيمة إنما يصار إليها للعجز عنه، والعجز في يوم الانقطاع، فيعتبر فيه وللثاني: أن المثل لما انقطع التحق بالقيمي، وفيه يعتبر القيمة يوم وللإمام أن المثل هو الواجب بالغصب، وهو باق في ذمته ما لم يقض القاضي، ولهذا لو صبر إلى أن يعود المثل كان. القضاء، وبقول الإمام قال مالك وأكثر الشافعية وحد الانقطاع: أن لا يوجد في السوق الغصب، له ذلك، فتعتبر قيمته يوم الذي يباع فيه وإن كان يوجد في البيوت. (تكملة، عيني) وما لا مثل له إلخ: أي إذا هلك المغصوب ولا مثل له كالحيوان والمذروعات والمعدودات المتفاوتة والوزني الذي يضره التبعيض، يجب على الغاصب قيمته يوم الغصب وهذا بالإجماع بين أئمتنا؛ لأنه تعذر اعتبار المثل صورة ومعنى وهو الكامل، فوجب اعتبار المثل معنى وهو القيمة؛ لأنها تقوم مقامه، ويحصل بها مثله، وقال الإمام مالك: يضمنه المثل صورة. (تكملة، عيني)
And it is obligatory to return the object in the place where he usurped it, i.e., the very substance of the usurped item, or its equivalent (mithl) if it perished and it is mithli (fungible), and if the mithl becomes unavailable then its value on the day of litigation; and what has no mithl like animals and countable items, its value on the day of usurpation. ... (full translation lengthy)...
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage lays out the primary obligation of the usurper: to return the exact object if it still exists, in the place where he took it. The proof is from Hadith: 'The hand must return what it has taken' and from the Quranic verse in Surah al-Baqarah (194) about recompense in kind. The text explains that returning the object is the original and most just remedy; if it perishes, the usurper must pay the mithl (exact equivalent for fungible goods). If the mithl is no longer available in the market (insirim al-mithl), there is a dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa says the value is on the day of litigation (yawm al-khusumah), Abu Yusuf says on the day of usurpation, and Muhammad says on the day the mithl becomes unavailable. The Hanafi position (Imam's view) is that the mithl remains a debt in the usurper's liability until the judge rules, and he may wait for its return. The majority of the school follow Imam Abu Hanifa. For non-mithli items like animals, the value is on the day of usurpation by consensus of the Hanafi imams, as the mithl is impossible; the value serves as a surrogate. The text also mentions that if the usurper returns the object without the owner's knowledge (e.g., gives it as a gift or feeds it to him), he is discharged, though feeding involves a dispute with Shafi'i.

Key Terms
مثلي (mithli): A fungible good that can be replaced by an identical unit (e.g., wheat, oil).
القيمة (al-qeemah): Monetary value paid when mithl is unavailable or for non-mithli goods.
انصرم المثل (insirim al-mithl): When the mithl of a fungible good is no longer available in the market (even if found in homes).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (mufta bihi), on which day is the value of a fungible good assessed after its mithl becomes unavailable?
A) Day of usurpation
B) Day the mithl became unavailable
C) Day of litigation
D) Day of the owner's choice

Key Takeaway
The usurper must return the object; if it perishes, pay the mithl; if mithl unavailable, pay value on litigation day (Hanafi position).

Claim of Destruction by Usurper: Detention and Evidence Preference
Ruling on judge detaining usurper claiming destruction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure when a usurper claims destruction, apply the detention rule, and distinguish the intra-Hanafi dispute between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding evidence preference.

Core Idea
A judge detains a usurper claiming destruction until convinced; evidence preference after return splits Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a common legal scenario: a usurper (ghasib) claims the property he took was destroyed. How does the court proceed? The Hanafi school provides a procedure of detention and evidence evaluation, with an internal school disagreement on whose proof prevails when the claim of destruction is made after an alleged return.

Guided Path
1
Identify the procedural ruling
Read the opening: the judge detains the usurper who claims destruction. Understand that this is a procedural detention to verify the truth.
The detention is analogous to detaining a debtor claiming insolvency.
2
Understand the rationale
The owner's right is attached to the property, so the usurper's claim is not accepted automatically. The judge must become convinced that the property is truly gone.
3
Examine the analogy (qiyas)
The passage compares this to the case of a debtor who claims insolvency. Both involve an obligation (return property or pay debt) and uncertainty about the claim.
This is a qiyas khafi (implicit analogy).
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
When the usurper claims destruction after returning the property and the owner denies return, Muhammad says the usurper's evidence is preferred; Abu Yusuf says the owner's evidence is preferred. Understand each imam's reasoning.
Muhammad focuses on the supervening factor (return); Abu Yusuf focuses on the original guarantee obligation.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If the usurper's evidence is accepted, he is not liable; if the owner's evidence is accepted, the usurper must pay the value.
The text does not specify which view is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن ادعى هلاكه حبسه الحاكم، حتى يعلم أنه لو بقي لأظهره، ثم قضى عليه ببدله، فإن ادعى هلاكه إلخ: أي إن أدعى الغاصب هلاك المغصوب حبسه الحاكم حتى يعلم أن المغصوب لو كان عنده لأظهره؛ لأن حق المالك ثابت في العين، فلا يقبل قوله فيه حتى يغلب على ظنه أنه صادق فيما يقول، كما إذا ادعى المديون الإفلاس، وليس الحبس حد مقدر، بل موكول إلى رأي القاضي كحبس الغريم بالدين، ولو ادعى الغاصب الهلاك عند صاحبه بعد الرد وعكس المالك، وأقاما البينة، فبينة الغاصب أولى عند محمد؛ لأنها تثبت الرد، وهو عارض، والبينة لمن يدعي العوارض، وعند أبي يوسف بينة المالك أولى؛ لأنها تثبت الضمان وجوباً والآخر منكر، والبينة للإثبات. [تكملة البحر الرائق: ۲۱۹/۸]
If he claims its destruction, the judge detains him until he knows that if it had remained he would have produced it, then he passes judgment against him for its replacement. 'If he claims its destruction etc.' means: if the usurper claims the destruction of the usurped property, the judge detains him until he knows that if the property had been with him he would have produced it; because the owner's right is established in the property, so his statement is not accepted until the judge's assumption that he is truthful prevails, as when a debtor claims insolvency. The detention has no fixed time limit but is entrusted to the judge's discretion, like detaining a debtor for a debt. If the usurper claims destruction after return and the owner contradicts, and both produce evidence, then according to Muhammad the evidence of the usurper is preferable because it establishes return, which is a supervening factor, and evidence is for the one who claims supervening factors. According to Abu Yusuf, the evidence of the owner is preferable because it establishes the obligation of guarantee, and the other is a denier, and evidence is for affirmation. [Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:219]
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the procedure when a usurper claims that the usurped property was destroyed. The Hanafi school holds that the judge detains the usurper until it becomes clear that the property is indeed gone, because the owner's right remains attached to the property. This is analogous to detaining a debtor who claims insolvency. The passage also presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on whose evidence is preferred when the usurper claims destruction after returning the property and the owner denies return. Muhammad says the usurper's evidence is stronger because return is a supervening factor (arid), and evidence is for the one who asserts supervening factors. Abu Yusuf says the owner's evidence is stronger because it establishes the obligation of guarantee, and the other party is a denier. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated, but the reasoning of both is presented.

Key Terms
الهلاك (al-halāk): Destruction of the usurped property so that the original cannot be returned.
الرد (ar-radd): Return of the usurped property to its owner.
البينة (al-bayyinah): Evidence presented in court; in this context, witnesses or proof of a claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad, whose evidence is preferred if the usurper claims destruction after returning the property and the owner denies?
A) The owner's evidence, because it establishes guarantee.
B) The usurper's evidence, because it establishes a supervening factor.
C) Both are equal, so no judgment.
D) The judge's personal knowledge is used.

Key Takeaway
When a usurper claims destruction, the judge detains him until convinced; if return is claimed, evidence preference depends on the imam (Muhammad vs. Abu Yusuf).

The Scope of Ghasp: Movable Property Only
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute on scope of ghasp

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ghasp (usurpation) and explain why immovable property is excluded, including the key proof and the practical consequence of the dispute.

Core Idea
Ghasp requires physical transfer; immovables cannot be moved, so no liability for destruction.

This lesson addresses the legal definition of ghasp (usurpation) and its scope in Hanafi law. The school restricts ghasp to movable property, a point of contention with other schools and even within the Hanafi madhhab. Understanding the reasoning behind this position clarifies a fundamental principle: the act of usurpation must involve physical transfer of possession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the Hanafi position
State that the Hanafi school holds that ghasp only applies to movable property, and a usurper of an immovable (like land or a house) is not liable for its destruction.
This is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa and later Abu Yusuf.
2
Understand the definition of ghasp
Ghasp is defined as 'removing the owner's hand by establishing one's own hand' (إزالة يد المالك بإثبات يده). This requires physical transfer of the property; it cannot happen with immovables.
The text uses a linguistic argument: the definite article 'al-' indicates restriction to the genus.
3
Examine the opposing argument
Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i argue that ghasp involves two characteristics: wrongful possession and removal of rightful possession; both can occur in immovables by occupying land. They analogize to a trustee (mudi') who guarantees an immovable by denying it.
Early Abu Yusuf also held this view.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis reject the analogy because the trustee's guarantee is based on breach of trust, not ghasp. Ghasp requires physical transfer, which is impossible for immovables. Expelling the owner is an act upon the owner, not the property.
The text concludes: 'At most, he can expel the owner from it, and that is an act upon the owner, not upon the property, so it does not necessitate guarantee.'
5
Note the practical consequence and tarjih
The thamarah al-khilaf: if an immovable is destroyed while in the usurper's hand, no liability in the Hanafi view; liability in the opposing view. The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's, but for waqf immovables, fatwa may follow Muhammad's view (liability).
This exception is noted from al-'Ayni.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والغصب فيما ينقل إلخ أي الغصب يتحقق فيما ينقل لا غير؛ لأنه إزالة يد المالك بإثبات يده، وذلك يتصور في المنقول لا غير، والقصر مستفاد من تعريف المبتدأ بلام الجنس؛ فإنه يفيد قصره في الخبر، ثم الغصب في المنقول يتحقق بالنقل ولا يتحقق بدونه على الصحيح لكن ما لم يتصرف فيه تصرف المالك، فإذا تصرف قيل: يكون غاصبا بدون النقل. لم يضمنه إلخ: أي لم يضمن الغاصب العقار؛ لما مر من أن الغصب لا يتحقق في العقار، وهذا عند الإمام وأبي يوسف، وقال محمد وزفر والشافعي يضمن وهو قول أبي يوسف أولا، وفي العيني: ويفتى في عقار الوقف بقول محمد. لهم: أن الغصب يتحقق بوصفين بإثبات اليد العادية وإزالة اليد المحقة، وذلك يمكن في العقار؛ لأن إثبات اليدين المتدافعتين على شيء واحد غير ممكن؛ لتعذر اجتماع نية، فإذا ثبت اليد العادية للغاصب انتفت اليد المحقة للمالك، ولهذا يضمن العقار المودع بالجحود، ولنا أن الغاصب تصرف في المغصوب بإثبات يده وإزالة يد المالك، ولا يكون ذلك إلا بالنقل والعقار لا يمكن نقله، وأقصى ما يكون فيه إخراج المالك منه، وذلك تصرف في المالك لا في العقار، فلا يوجب الضمان. [تكملة البحر الرائق: 220/8] (باختصار)
And ghasp is in what is moved etc.: i.e., ghasp occurs only in movable property because it is removing the owner's hand by establishing one's own hand, and that is conceivable only in movables. The restriction is derived from defining the subject with the definite article of genus, which indicates its restriction in the predicate. Then ghasp in movables occurs by physical transfer and not without it according to the correct view, but if he does not physically transfer it but acts like an owner, some say he becomes a usurper without transfer. 'He did not guarantee it etc.': i.e., the usurper does not guarantee the immovable because ghasp does not occur in immovables. This is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i say he does guarantee, and this was also Abu Yusuf's earlier view. In al-'Ayni: fatwa is given on waqf immovables according to Muhammad. Their argument: ghasp occurs with two characteristics: establishing wrongful possession and removing rightful possession, and this is possible in immovables because establishing two conflicting hands on one thing is impossible due to impossibility of combining intentions. So if the wrong hand of the usurper is established, the rightful hand of the owner is eliminated. For this reason, the trustee (mudi') guarantees an immovable by denial. Our argument: the usurper's action in the usurped property is by establishing his hand and removing the owner's hand, and that can only be done by physical transfer, and an immovable cannot be moved. At most, he can expel the owner from it, and that is an act upon the owner, not upon the property, so it does not necessitate guarantee. [Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:220] (abridged)
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof defining the scope of ghasp (usurpation). The Hanafi school holds that ghasp applies only to movable property because it requires physical transfer of possession, which is not possible for immovables. The proof is that ghasp is defined as removing the owner's hand by establishing one's own hand; this can only occur with physical transfer. Therefore, if someone seizes an immovable (real estate) and it is destroyed in his hand, he is not liable for its value. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (in their later view) hold this, while Muhammad and Zufar say it does apply to immovables, making him liable. The Shafi'i school agrees with Muhammad. The Hanafi argument is that transferring an immovable is impossible; one can only expel the owner, which acts on the owner, not on the property itself. The comment also notes that in waqf immovables, some give fatwa according to Muhammad's view.

Key Terms
الغصب (al-ghaṣb): Taking property by force, removing the owner's possession.
المنقول (al-manqūl): Movable property that can be physically transferred.
العقار (al-ʿiqār): Immovable property (real estate).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the Hanafi school restricts ghasp to movable property?
A) Because immovables are more valuable and require special rules.
B) Because ghasp requires physical transfer of possession, which is impossible for immovables.
C) Because the owner of immovables always retains some access.
D) Because there is no Quranic text on immovables.

Key Takeaway
Ghasp requires physical transfer; therefore, it applies only to movable property, with a notable exception in the fatwa for waqf immovables.
